                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$(D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math>) in H-OLHC-1300 °C and D-OLHC-1300 °C, kinetic analysis based on galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was utilized during the second discharge-charge process (Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0006">6f</a>, during the first stage of discharge potential (above 0.1V), the diffusion rate of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/647cbb17-f1b3-4727-bde0-1df72b080f1b/aenm202403142-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202403142:aenm202403142-math-0003" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202403142-math-0003.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mo>+</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> maintained at about 10<sup>−8.6–9.0</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup> in the sloping region, which shows higher diffusion kinetics compared with D-OLHC-1300 °C (10<sup>−9.0–10.4</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup>) in this region (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16e</a>, Supporting Information). The higher and faster <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/23ceed87-5c0c-49c5-b3bd-caa8a0a26be4/aenm202403142-math-0004.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202403142:aenm202403142-math-0004" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202403142-math-0004.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mo>+</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> kinetics in the sloping regions is highly beneficial to the high-rate performance and cycling stability of the H-OLHC-1300 °C. When the potential decreases between 0.1 and 0.05 V in the plateau region, the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/e3cb85ed-bd55-47a4-a5bd-b51e8baeefad/aenm202403142-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202403142:aenm202403142-math-0005" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202403142-math-0005.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mo>+</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> of H-OLHC-1300 °C gradually decreases to 10<sup>−8.6–9.1</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup> which is notably higher and faster than that in the plateau region of D-OLHC-1300 °C (10<sup>−10.4–11.3</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup>). The electrochemical reaction kinetics in both the slope and plateau zones are described here, which supports the idea that the sloping region is caused by fast <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/7611eaaf-afe6-4773-9255-fe05aab600ab/aenm202403142-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202403142:aenm202403142-math-0006" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202403142-math-0006.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mo>+</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> kinetics, which corresponds to the adsorption of Na<sup>+</sup> on the surface defects, and interlayer defects.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403142-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403142-bib-0027_R_d69166958e1560" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Energy Environ. Sci. Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/48aeb4ce-6321-402c-b6a3-dff113aa8c56/aenm202403142-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202403142:aenm202403142-math-0007" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202403142-math-0007.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msubsup>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>N</mi>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <mo>+</mo>
                     </msubsup>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$D_{Na}^ + $</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> gradually decreases in the plateau region of the hard carbon, due to the accumulation of the Na<sup>+,</sup>corresponding to the adsorption-interlayer intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>, within the bulk phase of hard carbon.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403142-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403142-bib-0040_R_d69166958e1580" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Energy Lett.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>In addition, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were conducted to investigate the interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> transfer kinetics in the cycled H-OLHC-1300 °C and D-OLHC-1300 °C electrode (anode fully sodiated) and the SEI layer evolution under the 1C cycling rate. Selected impedance spectra for H-OLHC-1300 °C and H-OLHC-1300 °C are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0006">6g,h</a>, in which a semicircle in the high-frequency region with small linear diffusion drift is identified in all these spectra, which distinguishes the similar non-faradaic process in H-OLHC-1300 °C and D-OLHC-1300 °C electrodes. The internal resistance, Rs (including electrolyte and electrode), and interfacial resistance including, R<sub>SEI</sub> and charge-transfer resistance, R<sub>ct</sub> in the high and medium frequency region are critical in determining how well Na<sup>+</sup> can be stored in an electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202403142-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202403142-bib-0004_R_d69166958e1601" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Natl. Sci. Rev. Adv. Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The fitting values of R<sub>s</sub>, R<sub>SEI</sub>, and R<sub>ct</sub> were quantified with an equivalent circuit presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0006">6i,j</a>, and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information). From the impedance results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0006">6g–j</a>), it has been shown that the R<sub>SEI</sub>, and R<sub>ct</sub> in H-OLHC-1300 °C are more stable (less than 15 Ohm) and greatly lower than those of D-OLHC-1300 °C after 500 cycles. For instance, after 100 cycles, the R<sub>SEI</sub>, and R<sub>ct</sub> for D-OLHC-1300 °C (103.3 and 113.2 Ohm) are 13.1 and 9.2 times that of H-OLHC-1300 °C (7.9 and 12.3 Ohm), respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0006">6j</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information), implying the stable and thinner SEI layer on H-OLHC-1300 °C electrode surface with remarkably enhanced interfacial charge transfer kinetics, compared with D-OLHC-1300 °C.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202403142-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202403142-sec-0070-title">2.5 Electrochemical Measurement of the H-OLHC-1300 °C||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Full-Cells</h3>
            
            <p>As a practical application, H-OLHC-1300 °C and D-OLHC-1300 °C have been used as anode coupling with Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode to prepare Na<sup>+</sup> full cells (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7a</a>) and measured at 30–3000 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> in a working voltage of 1.5–3.9 V. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7b</a>, demonstrate the comparative rate performance of the H-OLHC-1300 °C and D-OLHC-1300 °C assembled full cell. The H-OLHC-1300 °C||NVP full cell can deliver a high reversible capacity of 307.2 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a current density of 30 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (normalized by the active mass of anode), with an output working voltage of 3.4 V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7c</a>). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7c</a> shows the GCD profiles of H-OLHC-1300 °C||NVP, which together exhibit synergetic electrochemical processes between H-OLHC-1300 °C and NVP, where the plateau and sloping regions of the full cell match those of H-OLHC-1300 °C in the half cell. As the current density increased to 60, 150, 300, 600, 1500, and 3000 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, the H-OLHC-1300 °C||NVP full cell delivered an average capacity of 282.6, 257.9, 241.4, 221.3, 185.5 and 134.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, indicating exceptional rate performance and rapid charging capability. Moreover, reversing the current density back to 600 mA g<sup>−1</sup> restores the original capacity value, showcasing excellent reversibility in the capacity.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202403142-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/359bc624-f195-4d9b-a12c-dd4ffe9304d8/aenm202403142-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/359bc624-f195-4d9b-a12c-dd4ffe9304d8/aenm202403142-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/080e7d3c-d4b8-422f-bf8e-f5ee0be27cf4/aenm202403142-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/359bc624-f195-4d9b-a12c-dd4ffe9304d8/aenm202403142-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202403142-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202403142" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic of Na<sup>+</sup> full-cell configuration with H-OLHC-1300 °C anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode; b) Rate performance of the H-OLHC-1300 °C//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and D-OLHC-1300 °C//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full-cell at the current density of 30, 60, 150, 300, 600, 1500, and 3000 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and, c,d) corresponding GCD curves; e) Cycling stability at 600 mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, between H-OLHC-1300 °C//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and D-OLHC-1300 °C//Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>In comparison, the D-OLHC-1300 °C||NVP full cell showed a lower initial capacity of 258.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 30 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and poor rate performance with an average capacity retention of only 24.6% at 1500 mA g<sup>−1</sup> and completely degraded to 0.0023% capacity retention at 3000 mA g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7b,d</a>), as a result of the inferior electrochemical performance of D-OLHC-1300 °C. In addition, a well-stable capacity of ≈189.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 600 mA g<sup>−1</sup> over 200 cycles is delivered (83.3% capacity retention) by the H-OLHC-1300 °C||NVP full cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202403142-fig-0007">7e</a>), which is higher than those of D OLHC-1300 °C||NVP full cell (≈ 60.9%), demonstrating excellent cycling performance in practical application.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403142-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202403142-sec-0080-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we have demonstrated the critical role of the synthetic conditions (i.e., hydrothermal pre-carbonization, and direct carbonization) in regulating the structure and the electrochemical Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of hard carbon (HC) derived from oak leaves (OL) biowaste precursor (OLHC). Employing an advanced ex situ/in situ characterization combined with theoretical calculations reveals that pre-hydrothermal regulation of OLHC can stabilize the morphologies based on micro/mesoporous spherical particles with a compact packing density (0.72 g mL<sup>−1</sup>) and introduce additional active sites including defects, nanovoids, and surface-rich oxygenated groups, which shows uneven surface electrostatic potential and lower activation energy for Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption and generate a thin layer of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>/NaF-enriched core-shell-like SEI modulation with organic–inorganic composition, which in turn enables the fast interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and contributes to the high-capacity retention and stable cycling performance. As a result, the hydrothermal pretreated OLHC-derived anode (H-OLHC-1300 °C) can outperform those prepared by direct carbonization (D-OLHC-1300 °C) and demonstrated high-reversible capacity (378 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1 C), superior rate performance (272.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10 C), remarkable cycling performance (97%/88%/75% reversible capacity after 100/1200/8000 cycles at 0.1C/1 C/10 C) and decent ICE (85%). The study unveils the critical role of pre-hydrothermal carbonization strategy to regulate oak-leaves-bio waste and produce advanced hard carbons with true sustainability and improved performance for SIBs, thereby implying the possible useful step toward developing a new hard carbon from other biowaste precursors.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

The computations in this paper were run on the Siyuan-1 cluster supported by the Center for High-Performance Computing at Shanghai Jiao Tong University.</p>

      </div>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202403142-sec-0100">

         <p>The authors declare no conflict of interest.</p>
